# Paper Index

> Updated 2026-04-01. Covers 371 entries (all PDFs in `processed/`).

## Taxonomy Key

**Purpose:** Original Research | Meta-Analysis | Review | Instrument Validation | Commentary/Editorial | Book Chapter

**Methodology:** Cross-Sectional | Longitudinal | Twin/Genetic | Experience Sampling | Instrument Validation | Meta-Analysis | Systematic Review | Narrative Review | Experimental/Intervention | Mega-Analysis | Factor Analysis

**Instruments:** Named personality/cognitive measures used (e.g., NEO-PI-R, BFI-2, HEXACO-PI-R, BFAS, BESSI, etc.)

**Level of Detail:** Personality Domain | Personality Aspect | Personality Facet | Cognitive Ability | g | Item-Level | Other

---

## processed/ (formerly originals/)

### 1. Ashton_2007.pdf
- **Citation:** Ashton, M. C., & Lee, K. (2007). Empirical, theoretical, and practical advantages of the HEXACO model of personality structure. *Personality and Social Psychology Review*, *11*(2), 150–166. https://doi.org/10.1177/1088868306294907
- **Purpose:** Review
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** HEXACO-PI-R, NEO-PI-R, NEO-FFI
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** Prestige: XL | *Personality and Social Psychology Review*. HEXACO model advantages over Big Five.
- **Notes:** Argues the six-factor HEXACO model is a viable alternative to Big Five/FFM; reviews lexical studies across languages.
### 2. ashton_2009.pdf
- **Citation:** Ashton, M. C., & Lee, K. (2009). The HEXACO–60: A short measure of the major dimensions of personality. *Journal of Personality Assessment*, *91*(4), 340–345. https://doi.org/10.1080/00223890902935878
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis, Instrument Validation
- **Instruments:** HEXACO-60, HEXACO-PI-R, NEO-FFI
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 1,670 (2 samples) | Structural: M | HEXACO-60 short form development with college + community samples. Domain-level structure only. Single-country (Canadian).
- **Notes:** Development and psychometrics of the 60-item HEXACO short form; college student (n=936) and community adult (n=734) samples.
### 3. ashton_2016_hh.pdf
- **Citation:** Ashton, M. C., & Lee, K. (2016). Age trends in HEXACO-PI-R self-reports. *Journal of Research in Personality*, *64*, 102–111. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jrp.2016.08.008
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** HEXACO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 97,583 | Developmental: M · Structural: L | Massive N gives precise structural estimates. HEXACO, not NEO — facets don't map 1:1. Cross-sectional, so developmental claims are cohort-confounded. No regression coefficients reported, only approximate z-scores from figures.
- **Notes:** ~100,000 participants aged 14–74. Facet-level age trends diverge notably from domain-level trends, particularly within Emotionality and Extraversion.
### 4. bleidorn_2009.pdf
- **Citation:** Bleidorn, W., Kandler, C., Riemann, R., Angleitner, A., & Spinath, F. M. (2009). Patterns and sources of adult personality development: Growth curve analyses of the NEO PI-R scales in a longitudinal twin study. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*, *97*(1), 142–155. https://doi.org/10.1037/a0015434
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Longitudinal, Twin/Genetic, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 344 individuals (126 MZ, 61 DZ pairs) | Developmental: M · Heritability: S | Unique design: biometric growth curve modeling on all 30 NEO-PI-R facets across 3 waves. But severely underpowered (61 DZ pairs) for facet-level biometric decomposition. 84% female. Covers ages 18–59 only. Phenotypic developmental findings are more trustworthy than biometric estimates.
- **Notes:** Bielefeld Longitudinal Study of Adult Twins (BiLSAT); 126 MZ + 61 DZ pairs, 1995–2005. Biometric growth curve models for all 5 domains and 30 facets.
### 5. brandes_2020.pdf
- **Citation:** Brandes, C. M., Kushner, S. C., Herzhoff, K., & Tackett, J. L. (2020). Facet-level personality development in the transition to adolescence: Maturity, disruption, and gender differences. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*.
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Longitudinal
- **Instruments:** ICID-SF (Inventory of Child Individual Differences – Short Form)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 440 children | Developmental: L | Childhood sample (ages 9–13) with mother-report only. Non-NEO instrument (ICID-S, 15 facets). Latent growth models with measurement invariance tested. Some models failed to converge. Preadolescent developmental processes may not generalize to adults.
- **Notes:** Cohort-sequential design; 440 children at four annual timepoints (ages ~10–13). Mother-reported. Latent growth curve models for 15 facets.
### 6. brandt_etal_2023.pdf
- **Citation:** Brandt, N. D., Drewelies, J., Willis, S. L., Schaie, K. W., Ram, N., Gerstorf, D., & Wagner, J. (2023). Beyond Big Five trait domains: Stability and change in personality facets across midlife and old age. *Journal of Personality*, *91*(5), 1171–1188. https://doi.org/10.1111/jopy.12791
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Longitudinal, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 1,667 | Developmental: L | Strong latent modeling with scalar invariance; all 30 NEO-PI-R facets. Cannot separate age from period effects for mean-level change. Reliable estimates restricted to ages 35–80.
- **Notes:** Seattle Longitudinal Study; N=1,667 adults (M_age=62.69); four waves over 11 years. Facet-level rank-order stabilities and mean-level changes vary within the same domain.
### 7. briley_2012_hh.pdf
- **Citation:** Briley, D. A., & Tucker-Drob, E. M. (2012). Broad bandwidth or high fidelity? Evidence from the structure of genetic and environmental effects on the facets of the Five Factor Model. *Behavior Genetics*, *42*(5), 743–763. https://doi.org/10.1007/s10519-012-9548-8
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** CPI-Big Five (California Psychological Inventory Big Five facets)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 807 twin pairs | Structural: M · Heritability: M · Genetic correlations: S | Non-standard instrument (CPI-Big Five, 16 facets), adolescent sample (~17), high-achieving (NMSQT takers). Adventurousness loaded on A not O — sample-specific phenotypic anomaly.
- **Notes:** 490 MZ and 317 DZ twins from the National Merit Twin Study. Both domain-general and facet-specific genetic/environmental influences found.

### 7b. (no PDF — referenced in study_quality)
- **Citation:** Briley, D. A., & Tucker-Drob, E. M. (2014). Genetic and environmental continuity in personality development: A meta-analysis. *Psychological Bulletin*, *140*(5), 1303–1331. https://doi.org/10.1037/a0037091
- **Purpose:** Meta-Analysis
- **Methodology:** Meta-Analysis, Twin/Genetic, Longitudinal
- **Instruments:** Multiple (aggregated across 24 longitudinal twin studies)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain
- **Notes:** Meta-analysis of 21,057 sibling pairs. Genetic contributions to personality stability increase with age; environmental contributions also grow but more slowly. Domain-level only — no facet data.
### 8. cemalcilar_2021.pdf
- **Citation:** Cemalcilar, Z., Baruh, L., Kezer, M., Soto, C. J., Sumer, N., & John, O. P. (2021). Testing the BFI-2 in a non-WEIRD community sample. *Personality and Individual Differences*, *182*, 111087. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.paid.2021.111087
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Instrument Validation, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** BFI-2, BFI-2-S, BFI-2-XS, BFI, HEXACO
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 1,246 (2 studies) | Structural: M | Turkish BFI-2 adaptation with student + nationally representative community samples. Domain and facet structure replicated. Single country.
- **Notes:** Turkish adaptation; university and nationally representative community samples of young adults aged 18–35.
### 9. Danner_2019.pdf
- **Citation:** Danner, D., Rammstedt, B., Bluemke, M., Lechner, C., Berres, S., Knopf, T., Soto, C. J., & John, O. P. (2019). Das Big Five Inventar 2: Validierung eines Persönlichkeitsinventars zur Erfassung von 5 Persönlichkeitsdomänen und 15 Facetten. *Diagnostica*. https://doi.org/10.1026/0012-1924/a000218
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis, Instrument Validation
- **Instruments:** BFI-2, NEO-PI-R, BFI
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 1,224 | Structural: M | German BFI-2 validation with population survey sample. Measurement invariance by gender/age. Domain and facet reliabilities adequate. Single country.
- **Notes:** German BFI-2 validation (N=1,224 population survey); reliability, validity, measurement invariance by gender/age; German norms.
### 10. deyoung_2007.pdf
- **Citation:** DeYoung, C. G., Quilty, L. C., & Peterson, J. B. (2007). Between facets and domains: 10 aspects of the Big Five. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*, *93*(5), 880–896. https://doi.org/10.1037/0022-3514.93.5.880
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Factor Analysis, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R, AB5C-IPIP, IPIP, BFAS
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Aspect, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = ~2,500 (2 samples) | Structural: L | Foundational paper for 10-aspect model (BFAS); two independent samples with cross-validation from NEO-PI-R facets; aspects not facets.
- **Notes:** Foundational paper establishing the 10 Big Five Aspects and developing the BFAS (100 items). Aspects correspond to two genetic factors within each Big Five domain.
### 11. deyoung_2011.pdf
- **Citation:** Weisberg, Y. J., DeYoung, C. G., & Hirsh, J. B. (2011). Gender differences in personality across the ten aspects of the Big Five. *Frontiers in Psychology*, *2*, Article 178. https://doi.org/10.3389/fpsyg.2011.00178
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** BFAS, NEO-PI-R, IPIP
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Aspect
- **Quality:** N = ~900 | Structural: M | Gender differences across 10 Big Five aspects (BFAS); single sample; standard instrument (BFAS), moderate N, aspect-level only.
- **Notes:** Gender differences at aspect level that are masked at the domain level for Extraversion, Openness, and Conscientiousness. Filename refers to DeYoung as second author; first author is Weisberg.
### 12. eid_2003.pdf
- **Citation:** Eid, M., Riemann, R., Angleitner, A., & Borkenau, P. (2003). Sociability and positive emotionality: Genetic and environmental contributions to the covariation between different facets of extraversion. *Journal of Personality*, *71*(3), 319–346.
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** Multimethod self-report and other-report measures (not explicitly named)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 278 twin pairs | Structural: M · Heritability: M · Genetic correlations: M | Only Extraversion domain. Ad hoc 4-item composites from NEO-FFI, not standard NEO facets. Multi-method design (self, peer, situational affect) is a unique strength; modest N limits precision.
- **Notes:** 158 MZ and 120 DZ twin pairs. Strong genetic correlations between sociability and positive emotionality facets of Extraversion.
### 13. haehner_etal_2025_change.pdf
- **Citation:** Haehner, P., Krämer, M. D., Schaefer, B., Hopwood, C. J., & Bleidorn, W. (2025). Stability and change in lower-order personality traits in a representative Swiss sample. *European Journal of Personality*. https://doi.org/10.1177/08902070251405544
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Longitudinal, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** BFI-2
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Aspect
- **Quality:** N = 399 | CHILL Study; neuroticism intervention timing/context effects; personality domain-level; primarily an intervention process study.
- **Notes:** PERCIVAL study; N=4,495 Swiss adults, five waves over 2 years. High rank-order stabilities (r_avg ≈ .88/.87); mean-level changes differ across aspects within same domain.
### 14. haehner_etal_2025_validation.pdf
- **Citation:** Haehner, P., Krämer, M. D., Bleidorn, W., & Hopwood, C. J. (2026). Validating the Big Five Aspect Scales (BFAS) and the Short Form (BFAS-40) in German, French, and Italian. *Personality Science*, *6*, 1–22. https://doi.org/10.1177/27000710251391609
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Longitudinal, Instrument Validation, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** BFAS, BFAS-40
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Aspect
- **Quality:** N = 4,492 (5 waves) | Structural: L | BFAS and BFAS-40 validated in German, French, Italian (Swiss). Large probability sample with longitudinal data. Aspect-level (10 aspects), not facet-level.
- **Notes:** PERCIVAL project (N=4,492 Swiss adults). German, French, and Italian translations of full BFAS and BFAS-40.
### 15. hansen_2025.pdf
- **Citation:** Hansen, H. M. U., Laeng, B., Vassend, O. M., Czajkowski, N. O., Endestad, T., Danielsen, A., & Røysamb, E. (2025). The role of Big Five personality domains and facets in musical sensibility: A twin study. *Scientific Reports*, *15*, 13559. https://doi.org/10.1038/s41598-025-95661-z
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** BFI-2
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 2,592 (616 complete pairs) | Heritability: M · Genetic correlations: M | BFI-2 facets (not NEO). Only 2 facets entered biometric models (O2, A1). Primarily a musical sensibility paper that happens to use personality as input — selective facet coverage.
- **Notes:** Norwegian twin sample (N=2,592). Genetic influences accounted for 50–100% of personality–musical sensibility covariance. Aesthetic sensitivity facet of Open-mindedness was a strong predictor.
### 16. jackson_2009.pdf
- **Citation:** Jackson, J. J., Walton, K. E., Harms, P. D., Bogg, T., Wood, D., Lodi-Smith, J., Edmonds, G. W., & Roberts, B. W. (2009). Not all conscientiousness scales change alike: A multimethod, multisample study of age differences in the facets of conscientiousness. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*, *96*(2), 446–459. https://doi.org/10.1037/a0014156
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 274 (S1); 613 (S2) | Developmental: M · Structural: M | Conscientiousness only, non-standard facet system (Roberts 5-facet model). Study 2 is representative (Illinois) but 18.5% response rate. Observer-report in Study 1 is a strength. Coarse age grouping (3 bins) limits developmental precision.
- **Notes:** Two samples (N=274 community; N=613 statewide), ages 18–94. Five conscientiousness facets show divergent age trajectories.
### 17. jang_1996.pdf
- **Citation:** Jang, K. L., Livesley, W. J., & Vernon, P. A. (1996). Heritability of the Big Five personality dimensions and their facets: A twin study. *Journal of Personality*, *64*(3), 577–591.
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 250 twin pairs | Heritability: M | Small sample underpowered for nonadditive effects; univariate models only — no genetic correlations between facets. All 30 NEO-PI-R facets. Foundational but estimates are imprecise.
- **Notes:** 123 MZ and 127 DZ pairs. Domain heritability 41–61%. Shared environment negligible. Some facets show nonadditive genetic influence.
### 18. jang_1998.pdf
- **Citation:** Jang, K. L., McCrae, R. R., Angleitner, A., Riemann, R., & Livesley, W. J. (1998). Heritability of facet-level traits in a cross-cultural twin sample: Support for a hierarchical model of personality. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*, *74*(6), 1556–1565.
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 998 twin pairs (Canada + Germany) | Heritability: L | Two independent samples (Canada, Germany); all 30 NEO-PI-R facets with both raw and residual (domain-partialled) heritability. Residual heritability design is unique and informative. Larger than Jang 1996 but still univariate.
- **Notes:** Canadian (183 MZ, 175 DZ) and German (435 MZ, 205 DZ) twins. Additive genetic effects account for 25–65% of reliable specific facet variance. Supports hierarchical model where facets are discrete, biologically based constructs.
### 19. jang_2001.pdf
- **Citation:** Jang, K. L., Livesley, W. J., Angleitner, A., Riemann, R., Hu, S., Ando, J., Ono, Y., Vernon, P. A., & Hamer, D. H. (2001). Covariance structure of Neuroticism and Agreeableness: A twin and molecular genetic analysis of the role of the serotonin transporter gene. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*, *81*(2), 295–304. https://doi.org/10.1037/0022-3514.81.2.295
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 1,475 twin pairs + 388 sibling pairs | Structural: L · Heritability: L · Genetic correlations: L | Three independent samples (Canada, Germany, Japan) strengthen genetic findings. N and A facets only (12 of 30). Molecular component (5-HTTLPR) is a single candidate gene — small effects.
- **Notes:** 913 MZ and 562 DZ twins (Canada, Germany, Japan) + 388 nontwin siblings (US). 5-HTTLPR accounted for ~10% of the genetic relationship between N and A.
### 20. jang_etal_2002.pdf
- **Citation:** Jang, K. L., Livesley, W. J., Angleitner, A., Riemann, R., & Vernon, P. A. (2002). Genetic and environmental influences on the covariance of facets defining the domains of the five-factor model of personality. *Personality and Individual Differences*, *33*(1), 83–101. https://doi.org/10.1016/S0191-8869(01)00137-4
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 1,255 twin pairs (Canada + Germany) | Structural: L · Heritability: L · Genetic correlations: L | All 30 NEO-PI-R facets with multivariate models within each domain — genetic factor structure reported. Two independent samples strengthen findings. But analyses are domain-by-domain (6 facets at a time), so cross-domain genetic overlap is invisible. Self-report only.
- **Notes:** Canadian (253 MZ, 207 DZ) and German (526 MZ, 269 DZ) twins. Multiple genetic and environmental factors common to facets within each domain.
### 21. kim_etal_2017.pdf
- **Citation:** Kim, S. E., Yun, H.-N., Heo, S. G., Cho, J., Kwon, M.-J., Chang, Y., Ryu, S., Shin, H., Shin, C., Cho, N. H., Sung, Y. A., & Kim, H.-L. (2017). Meta-analysis of genome-wide SNP- and pathway-based associations for facets of neuroticism. *Journal of Human Genetics*, *62*, 903–909. https://doi.org/10.1038/jhg.2017.61
- **Purpose:** Meta-Analysis
- **Methodology:** Meta-Analysis
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R (Korean version)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 5,584 | Genetic correlations: S | Small for GWAS; only 1 SNP reached genome-wide significance. N facets only. Korean-only, no replication. Pathway-based analysis is the novel contribution but exploratory.
- **Notes:** GWAS meta-analysis (N=5,584) of six neuroticism facets across three Korean cohorts. Genome-wide significant SNP for angry hostility; axon guidance and focal adhesion pathways implicated.
### 22. LeCorff_2016.pdf
- **Citation:** Le Corff, Y., & Busque-Carrier, M. (2016). Structural validity of the NEO Personality Inventory 3 (NEO-PI-3) in a French-Canadian sample. *International Journal of Arts & Sciences*, *9*(03), 461–472.
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis, Instrument Validation
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-3, NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 1,313 | Structural: M | NEO-PI-3 French-Canadian validation. Only 13/30 facets show acceptable single-factor fit. Single sample, single language.
- **Notes:** French-Canadian sample (n=1,313). Acceptable CFA fit only under partial CFA; 13 of 30 facets showed acceptable single-factor fit.
### 23. lewis_bates_2014.pdf
- **Citation:** Lewis, G. J., & Bates, T. C. (2014). How genes influence personality: Evidence from multi-facet twin analyses of the HEXACO dimensions. *Journal of Research in Personality*, *51*, 9–17. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jrp.2014.04.004
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** HEXACO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 948 twin pairs + 1,202 singletons | Structural: M · Heritability: M · Genetic correlations: M | HEXACO-60 (not NEO) with very short facet scales (2–3 items, α as low as .38). ~90% female. Multivariate genetic models within each of 6 HEXACO domains. Low reliability compresses facet-specific variance, likely underestimating genetic differentiation. Older sample (M age 61).
- **Notes:** Multi-facet genetic analyses of all six HEXACO dimensions.
### 24. luciano_2005.pdf
- **Citation:** Luciano, M., Wainwright, M. A., Wright, M. J., & Martin, N. G. (2006). The heritability of conscientiousness facets and their relationship to IQ and academic achievement. *Personality and Individual Differences*, *40*(7), 1189–1199. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.paid.2005.10.013
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Facet, Cognitive Ability
- **Quality:** N = 431 families (~774 individuals) | Heritability: M · Genetic correlations: M | Conscientiousness facets only (6 of 30). Multivariate Cholesky with IQ is valuable but adolescent sample (M age 20), and low power to resolve A vs. D components.
- **Notes:** Adolescent twins/siblings. Heritabilities 0.18–0.49 for conscientiousness facets. General additive genetic factor across facets, IQ, and academic achievement.
### 25. ludeke_2019.pdf
- **Citation:** Ludeke, S. G., Bainbridge, T. F., Liu, J., Zhao, K., Smillie, L. D., & Zettler, I. (2019). Using the Big Five Aspect Scales to translate between the HEXACO and Big Five personality models. *Journal of Personality*, *87*(5), 1025–1038. https://doi.org/10.1111/jopy.12453
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** BFAS, HEXACO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Aspect, Personality Domain
- **Quality:** N = 1,586 (4 samples) | Structural: L | Four independent samples strengthen structural findings, but moderate total N and no correction for unreliability. Aspect-level only (BFAS), not NEO facets.
- **Notes:** BFAS as a bridge between HEXACO and Big Five frameworks.
### 26. misiuro_etal_2022.pdf
- **Citation:** Misiuro, T., Gorbaniuk, O., Macheta, K., McNeill, M., Kubicka-Jakuczun, J., Kuźmik, M., Wontor, P., Zajkowska, M., Rykowska, K., Świątek, P., & Zygnerska, M. (2022). Validation and psychometric properties of the HEXACO Personality Inventory observer report form in the Polish language. *Journal of Personality Assessment*, *104*(6), 844–854. https://doi.org/10.1080/00223891.2021.1998081
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Instrument Validation, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** HEXACO-PI-R (observer report form)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 666 | Structural: S | HEXACO-PI-R observer report in Polish. PCA yields 7 components rather than 6. Attitude toward target contaminates structure.
- **Notes:** Polish-language validation of the HEXACO observer report form.
### 27. mitrovik_2024.pdf
- **Citation:** Mitrović, D., Smederevac, S., Delgado-Cruzata, L., Sadiković, S., Pajić, D., Prinz, M., Budimlija, Z., Oljača, M., Kušić-Tišma, J., Vučinić, N., & Milutinović, A. (2024). Personality and *COMT* gene: molecular-genetic and epigenetic associations with NEO-PI-R personality domains and facets in monozygotic twins. *Frontiers in Genetics*, *15*, 1455872. https://doi.org/10.3389/fgene.2024.1455872
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 430 (SNP); 35 MZ pairs (epigenetic) | Genetic correlations: S | Single candidate gene (COMT V158M) with small effects (d≈0.15–0.21). Epigenetic sample is 35 pairs with no multiple-testing correction. NEO-PI-R α=.30 for Openness in this sample. Hypothesis-generating only.
- **Notes:** DNA methylation of COMT promoter region and NEO-PI-R associations in MZ twins. Epigenetic focus.
### 28. nikalosavic_2021.pdf
- **Citation:** Nikolašević, Ž., Dinić, B. M., Smederevac, S., Sadiković, S., Milovanović, I., Bugarski Ignjatović, V., Prinz, M., Budimlija, Z., & Zgonjanin Bosić, D. (2021). Common genetic basis of the five factor model facets and intelligence: A twin study. *Personality and Individual Differences*, *175*, 110682. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.paid.2021.110682
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R, Raven's Advanced Progressive Matrices
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet, g
- **Quality:** N = 212 twin pairs (424 individuals) | Heritability: S · Genetic correlations: S | Small twin sample underpowered for facet-level genetic correlations. Education-restricted, Serbian sample. All 30 NEO-PI-R facets but wide CIs on rG estimates.
- **Notes:** 424 twins (134 MZ pairs) from Serbian Twin Registry. Seven facets predict g; higher genetic (0.52) than environmental (0.13) correlations.
### 29. Ornfjord_2018_t2.pdf
- **Citation:** *[Incomplete — file is a single extracted table only]*
- **Purpose:** Unknown
- **Methodology:** Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** HEXACO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Notes:** Single-page table showing HEXACO factor/facet loadings, alpha, means, SDs (n=480). No title page or abstract.

### 30. Ørnfjord_2018.pdf
- **Citation:** Ørnfjord, M. (2018). The Norwegian HEXACO-PI-R: Psychometric properties and relationships with the Big Five Inventory. *Psykologisk.no*, sp/2018/12/e15. https://psykologisk.no/sp/2018/12/e15
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Instrument Validation, Factor Analysis, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** HEXACO-PI-R, BFI, NEO-PI-R, NEO-FFI
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 480 | Structural: S | Norwegian HEXACO-PI-R validation. Small N for 25-facet instrument. Single sample, single country.
- **Notes:** Norwegian HEXACO-PI-R validation; discusses overlap and distinctions with FFM.
### 31. pilia_etal_2006.pdf
- **Citation:** Pilia, G., Chen, W.-M., Scuteri, A., Orrù, M., Albai, G., Dei, M., ... & Schlessinger, D. (2006). Heritability of cardiovascular and personality traits in 6,148 Sardinians. *PLoS Genetics*, *2*(8), e132. https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pgen.0020132
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic, Cross-Sectional, Mega-Analysis
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 6,148 (711 pedigrees) | Heritability: XL · Genetic correlations: L | Large pedigree design can separate additive from dominance effects better than standard twins. All 30 NEO-PI-R facets. Sardinian founder population — genetically homogeneous, uncertain generalizability.
- **Notes:** Sardinian founder-population cohort (N=6,148; 34,469 relative pairs). Heritability for 98 traits including 35 personality traits.
### 32. Rammstedt_2018.pdf
- **Citation:** Rammstedt, B., Lechner, C. M., & Danner, D. (2018). Relationships between personality and cognitive ability: A facet-level analysis. *Journal of Intelligence*, *6*(2), 28. https://doi.org/10.3390/jintelligence6020028

- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** BFI-2
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet, Cognitive Ability, g
- **Quality:** N = 365 | Structural: M | BFI-2 facets and cognitive ability; facet-level analysis but single sample, modest N.
- **Notes:** German adults (N=365). Facets explain more variance than domains in cognitive ability; facets within the same domain can have suppressing associations.
### 33. Rammstedt_2026.pdf
- **Citation:** Rammstedt, B., Vogel, V., Roth, M., & Lechner, C. (2026). Unpacking the personality–cognitive ability link: A cross-national facet-level analysis of the Big Five. *Large-scale Assessments in Education*, *14*, 6. https://doi.org/10.1186/s40536-026-00281-2

- **Notes:** First cross-national facet-level study using PIAAC data from 12 countries. Facets account for ~2× the variance of domains (R²=0.10 vs 0.06).
### 34. ringwald_etal_2024.pdf
- **Citation:** Ringwald, W. R., Kaurin, A., Lawson, K. M., Wright, A. G. C., & Robins, R. W. (2024). The development of personality—from metatraits to facets—across adolescence and into adulthood in a sample of Mexican-origin youth. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*, *126*(6), 1140–1160. https://doi.org/10.1037/pspp0000487

- **Instruments:** BFI (or similar)

- **Quality:** N = 645 | Developmental: L | Strong design (5 waves across adolescence), but instrument switch at age 19 (BFI→BFI-2), low facet reliabilities (median ω=.60), and BFI-2 facets (15) not NEO facets (30). Single sociocultural context (Mexican-origin, low-SES).
- **Notes:** Mexican-origin youth (N=645) assessed 5 times from ages 14–23. Personality change at metatrait, domain, and facet levels simultaneously.
### 35. roberts_2005.pdf

### 36. romano_2023.pdf

### 37. roysamb_2018.pdf
- **Citation:** Røysamb, E., Nes, R. B., Czajkowski, N. O., & Vassend, O. (2018). Genetics, personality and wellbeing: A twin study of traits, facets and life satisfaction. *Scientific Reports*, *8*, 12298. https://doi.org/10.1038/s41598-018-29881-x

- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R, SWLS
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 1,516 twins | Heritability: M · Genetic correlations: M | Had full NEO-PI-R on 1,516 twins but only ran biometric models on 4 selected facets (N1, N3, E4, E6). Narrow age range (50–65). Missed opportunity for comprehensive facet heritability.
- **Notes:** Norwegian twins (N=1,516, ages 50–65). Facets accounted for 32% of life satisfaction variance vs. 24% for domains. Anxiety, depression, activity, and positive emotions most important.
### 38. Schimmack_2004.pdf
- **Citation:** Schimmack, U., Oishi, S., Furr, R. M., & Funder, D. C. (2004). Personality and life satisfaction: A facet-level analysis. *Personality and Social Psychology Bulletin*, *30*(8), 1062–1075. https://doi.org/10.1177/0146167204264292

### 39. schwaba_etal_2022.pdf

- **Notes:** Preregistered; US adults ages 30–70 (N=1,785) over 11–16 years. 47 facets; most matured adaptively but three healthy facets declined.
### 40. seifert_2023.pdf

- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain
- **Quality:** N = 48,264 (3 panels) | Developmental: XL | Gold-standard within-person design (fixed effects eliminates all stable between-person confounds). Three independent samples replicate. Domain- and item-level only — no facets. Short instruments (3–10 items/trait).
- **Notes:** Uses within-person (not between-person) change to estimate age trajectories from three large panels.

### 41. soto_etal_2011.pdf

- **Notes:** N=1,267,218 ages 10–65. Facets within the same domain often show distinct age trends.
### 42. soto_john_2012.pdf

- **Instruments:** BFI, NEO-PI-R

- **Notes:** Cross-sectional (N=601) + longitudinal (N=125 women). Adult development driven by narrowly acting mechanisms affecting individual facets.
### 43. soto_john_2017.pdf
- **Citation:** Soto, C. J., & John, O. P. (2017). The next Big Five Inventory (BFI-2): Developing and assessing a hierarchical model with 15 facets to enhance bandwidth, fidelity, and predictive power. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*, *113*(1), 117–143. https://doi.org/10.1037/pspp0000096

- **Instruments:** BFI-2, BFI

- **Quality:** N = ~3,600 (3 studies + validation) | Structural: XL | Definitive BFI-2 development paper with convergent validity against NEO PI-R, BFAS, and IPIP. Multiple independent samples. BFI-2 has 15 facets (not 30 NEO), deliberately excludes interstitial content. No heritability or developmental data.
- **Notes:** Three-study program developing the BFI-2. Hierarchical model with 5 domains and 15 facets (3 per domain). Foundational paper for the BFI-2.
### 44. stanek_ones_2023.pdf

- **Notes:** 60,690 personality–ability correlations from 3,543 meta-analyses. Covers hierarchical levels (factors, aspects, facets) and 97 cognitive ability constructs.
### 45. Sun_et_al_2017.pdf

### 46. Terracciano_2005.pdf

### 47. yamagata_etal_2006.pdf
- **Citation:** Yamagata, S., Suzuki, A., Ando, J., Ono, Y., Kijima, N., Yoshimura, K., Ostendorf, F., Angleitner, A., Riemann, R., Spinath, F. M., Livesley, W. J., & Jang, K. L. (2006). Is the genetic structure of human personality universal? A cross-cultural twin study from North America, Europe, and Asia. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*, *90*(6), 987–998. https://doi.org/10.1037/0022-3514.90.6.987
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** NEO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Quality:** N = 1,910 twin pairs (Canada, Germany, Japan) | Structural: XL · Genetic correlations: L | Three-country replication of genetic Big Five factor structure using all 30 NEO-PI-R facets. Gold-standard for structural claims about genetic vs. environmental factor organization. Does NOT report univariate heritability per facet. Japanese sample is much younger and more restricted in age range.
- **Notes:** 1,209 MZ and 701 DZ pairs from Canada, Germany, Japan. High congruence of phenotypic, genetic, and environmental factor structures across cultures.
### 48. zakrisson_etal_2025.pdf

BFI-2 (15 facets) not NEO (30). No heritability or developmental data. Studies 1–2 heavily skewed female and university-educated.
- **Notes:** Swedish BFI-2 adaptation and validation. Three samples (N=824, 1,104, 823). Predictive validity for well-being, attachment, SDO, ambivalent sexism.

- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability, g
- **Quality:** N = 86 samples | Structural: L | WM-g true-score r = .479, far from unity. Distinguishes WM from STM. n-back tasks show lower g correlations than complex span. No personality data.
- **Notes:** 86 samples. WM–g average true-score correlation = .479 (not unity); WM ≠ g; WM ≠ Gf; STM–g (.260) < WM–g (.397). Verbal WM tasks correlate more with g than spatial WM tasks; n-back tasks show lower correlations with g than complex span tasks.
### 103. ackerman_kanfer_2025.pdf
- **Citation:** Ackerman, P. L., & Kanfer, R. (2025). Cognitive ability and non-ability trait predictors of academic achievement: A four-year longitudinal study. *Journal of Intelligence*, *13*, 79. https://doi.org/10.3390/jintelligence13070079
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Longitudinal
- **Instruments:** CogAT, NEO-FFI, TIE, MTQ, UNIACT, self-concept/self-estimates of ability, domain knowledge tests
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Cognitive Ability
- **Quality:** N = 910 | Not a personality structure study; tests PPIK trait complex framework predicting academic achievement; personality measured at domain level only (NEO-FFI).
- **Notes:** N=910 9th-graders followed to 12th grade. Cognitive abilities predict 15–50% of variance in 12th-grade outcomes. Personality (Openness, TIE, Need for Achievement) adds modest incremental validity (~5–10%) after abilities. PPIK "trait complex" framework. Supplement file: ackerman_kanfer_2025_supp.pdf (full correlation matrix).
### 104. eronen-bringmann-2021_theory.pdf
- **Citation:** Eronen, M. I., & Bringmann, L. F. (2021). The theory crisis in psychology: How to move forward. *Perspectives on Psychological Science*, *16*(4), 779–788. https://doi.org/10.1177/1745691620970586
- **Purpose:** Commentary/Editorial
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Other
- **Quality:** Prestige: L | *Perspectives on Psychological Science*. Theory crisis in psychology.
- **Notes:** Three obstacles to good psychological theory: (1) lack of robust phenomena, (2) construct validity problems and epistemic iteration, (3) difficulty identifying causal relationships ("fat-handed" interventions). Argues psychology must establish robust phenomena before building elaborate theories.
### 105. graham_2012.pdf
- **Citation:** Graham, E. K., & Lachman, M. E. (2012). Personality stability is associated with better cognitive performance in adulthood: Are the stable more able? *Journals of Gerontology, Series B: Psychological Sciences and Social Sciences*, *67*(5), 545–554. https://doi.org/10.1093/geronb/gbr149

- **Instruments:** MIDUS personality scales, BTACT (Brief Test of Adult Cognition by Telephone)

- **Notes:** N=4,974 MIDUS participants. Personality stability (especially low N, high O) associated with better cognitive performance. Stability more beneficial than change in either direction. Neuroticism increase × age interaction: older adults who increased in N had worse reaction time.
### 106. kanfer_ackerman_1989_motivation.pdf
- **Citation:** Kanfer, R., & Ackerman, P. L. (1989). Motivation and cognitive abilities: An integrative/aptitude–treatment interaction approach to skill acquisition. *Journal of Applied Psychology*, *74*(4), 657–690. https://doi.org/10.1037/0021-9010.74.4.657
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Experimental/Intervention
- **Instruments:** ASVAB, Kanfer–Ackerman Air Traffic Controller (ATC) task, self-report measures
- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability, g
- **Quality:** N = 1,010 | Motivation-ability interaction in skill acquisition; ATC task; not a personality study.
- **Notes:** 3 experiments, 1,010 U.S. Air Force trainees. Integrates attentional resource framework with motivational processes during skill acquisition (declarative → knowledge compilation → procedural). Goal-setting reduces ability–performance correlations during declarative phase but enhances performance during procedural phase. General ability correlations decline with practice; perceptual speed correlations increase then decrease.
### 107. kanfer_ackerman_2004_motivation.pdf
- **Citation:** Kanfer, R., & Ackerman, P. L. (2004). Aging, adult development, and work motivation. *Academy of Management Review*, *29*(3), 440–458. https://doi.org/10.5465/amr.2004.13670969
- **Purpose:** Review
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability, Personality Domain
- **Quality:** Prestige: M | *Academy of Management Review*. Aging, adult development, and work motivation.
- **Notes:** Integrates life-span developmental research with work motivation theory. Four patterns of age-related change: loss (Gf decline), growth (Gc increase), reorganization (personality/motive restructuring), exchange (shift from performance to identity motives). Maps these to Kanfer's (1987) expectancy model via effort-performance, performance-utility, and effort-utility functions.
### 108. menon_2016_networks.pdf
- **Citation:** Menon, B. (2019). Towards a new model of understanding – The triple network, psychopathology and the structure of the mind. *Medical Hypotheses*, *133*, 109385. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.mehy.2019.109385
- **Purpose:** Commentary/Editorial

- **Level of Detail:** Other
- **Quality:** Prestige: S | *Medical Hypotheses*. Triple network model and psychopathology.
- **Notes:** Triple network model (Salience Network, Central Executive Network, Default Mode Network) applied to psychiatric disorders. Hypothesizes that harmonious functioning of these three networks constitutes "the mind." Table 1 maps disorders (schizophrenia, depression, OCD, anxiety, dissociative, addictions) to patterns of network dysfunction and reversibility.
### 109. Stanovich_2011_Handbook.pdf
- **Citation:** Stanovich, K. E. (2012). On the distinction between rationality and intelligence: Implications for understanding individual differences in reasoning. In K. J. Holyoak & R. G. Morrison (Eds.), *The Oxford Handbook of Thinking and Reasoning* (pp. 433–455). Oxford University Press. https://doi.org/10.1093/oxfordhb/9780199734689.013.0022
- **Purpose:** Book Chapter
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability, Other
- **Quality:** Prestige: XL | *Oxford Handbook of Thinking and Reasoning*. Tripartite model (autonomous/algorithmic/reflective mind). Foundational framework.
- **Notes:** Tripartite model of mind: autonomous (Type 1), algorithmic (Type 2 computational), reflective (Type 2 dispositional). IQ tests measure algorithmic-level processing but miss reflective-level thinking dispositions and mindware gaps. Framework for predicting when biases will vs. won't correlate with intelligence.
### 110. Stanovich_Toplak_2024_conspiracy.pdf
- **Citation:** Stanovich, K. E., & Toplak, M. E. (2024). Conspiracy beliefs in the context of a comprehensive rationality assessment. *Thinking & Reasoning*. https://doi.org/10.1080/13546783.2024.2368026
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** CART, Generic Conspiracist Beliefs Scale, AOT
- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability, Other
- **Quality:** N = 747 | CART and conspiracy beliefs; rationality assessment; not a personality study.
- **Notes:** N=747 adults. Superstitious thinking, actively open-minded thinking, and probabilistic reasoning are strongest predictors of conspiracy beliefs. Conspiracy beliefs more related to contaminated mindware and thinking dispositions than to cognitive ability per se.
### 111. Stanovich_West_1998.pdf
- **Citation:** Stanovich, K. E., & West, R. F. (1998). Individual differences in rational thought. *Journal of Experimental Psychology: General*, *127*(2), 161–188. https://doi.org/10.1037/0096-3445.127.2.161
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** SAT (cognitive ability proxy), various heuristics-and-biases tasks, AOT, Need for Cognition
- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability
- **Quality:** N = ~954 | Individual differences in rational thought; H&B tasks and cognitive ability; not a personality study.
- **Notes:** 4 studies, N≈954. Cognitive ability correlates with some H&B tasks (belief bias, argument evaluation) but not others (outcome bias, sunk cost). Thinking dispositions predict H&B performance beyond cognitive ability. Establishes the empirical program for individual differences in rational thinking.
### 112. Stanovich_West_2008.pdf
- **Citation:** Stanovich, K. E., & West, R. F. (2008). On the relative independence of thinking biases and cognitive ability. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*, *94*(4), 672–695. https://doi.org/10.1037/0022-3514.94.4.672
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** SAT, various bias tasks
- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability
- **Quality:** N = ~1,000+ (7 studies) | Independence of thinking biases from cognitive ability; not a personality study.
- **Notes:** 7 studies. Many thinking biases are uncorrelated with cognitive ability. Distinguishes 3 processing error types: (1) performance errors (ability-correctable), (2) mindware gaps (knowledge-correctable), (3) override failures (resist ability because they require sustained inhibition). Key theoretical framework for the intelligence–rationality dissociation.
### 113. Stanovich_West_Toplak_2011_devpsych.pdf
- **Citation:** Stanovich, K. E., West, R. F., & Toplak, M. E. (2011). The complexity of developmental predictions from dual process models. *Developmental Review*, *31*, 103–118. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.dr.2011.07.003
- **Purpose:** Review
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability
- **Quality:** Prestige: M | *Developmental Review*. Complexity of developmental predictions from dual-process models.
- **Notes:** Tripartite model applied to development. Five factors determine normative responding at a given age. Developmental predictions from dual-process theories are more complex than commonly realized; U-shaped developmental functions possible for some tasks depending on whether autonomous-mind learned associations align with normatively correct responses.
### 114. stanovich_west_toplak_2013_myside.pdf
- **Citation:** Stanovich, K. E., West, R. F., & Toplak, M. E. (2013). Myside bias, rational thinking, and intelligence. *Current Directions in Psychological Science*, *22*(4), 259–264. https://doi.org/10.1177/0963721413480174
- **Purpose:** Review
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability
- **Quality:** Prestige: M | *Current Directions in Psychological Science*. Myside bias, rational thinking, and intelligence.
- **Notes:** Myside bias is largely independent of cognitive ability. Critical distinction: when tasks explicitly instruct decontextualization (formal reasoning), intelligence correlates with avoiding bias; when they don't (naturalistic reasoning), intelligence provides no inoculation. Myside bias is a rational thinking skill missing from IQ tests.
### 115. Teovanović_2015.pdf
- **Citation:** Teovanović, P., Knežević, G., & Stankov, L. (2015). Individual differences in cognitive biases: Evidence against one-factor theory of rationality. *Intelligence*, *50*, 75–86. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.intell.2015.02.008

- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability, g
- **Quality:** N = 243 | Cognitive biases and rationality; NEO-FFI Openness used as predictor; not a personality structure study.
- **Notes:** N=243. Seven cognitive biases assessed; low inter-bias correlations. EFA yields 2 factors (normative irrationality, ecological rationality). Biases relatively independent of Gf, Gc, CRT, Openness, and NFC. Evidence against a single "rationality quotient."
### 116. toplak_stanovich_2024_art-y.pdf

### 131. westbrook_braver_2016.pdf

### 133. Pessiglione_2025.pdf
- **Citation:** Pessiglione, M., Blain, B., Wiehler, A., & Naik, S. (2025). Origins and consequences of cognitive fatigue. *Trends in Cognitive Sciences*, *29*(8), 730–749. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.tics.2025.02.005

- **Notes:** MetaMotiF (metabolico-motivational) model of cognitive fatigue. Fatigue arises from metabolic alterations in PFC (glutamate accumulation), increasing cognitive control cost. Key behavioral marker: "choice bias" toward low-effort/immediate-reward options, not self-report or performance decline.

- **Topic:** Motivation/Effort
- **Quality:** Prestige: XL | *Trends in Cognitive Sciences*. Why cognitive effort is experienced as costly.
- **Notes:** Three frameworks for why cognitive effort is costly: (1) architectural constraints/processing bottlenecks, (2) information-theoretic (KL divergence), (3) brain network control theory. Uses N-back as common reference; proposes RNN simulations to test accounts.
### 136. sandra_otto_2018.pdf
- **Citation:** Sandra, D. A., & Otto, A. R. (2018). Cognitive capacity limitations and Need for Cognition differentially predict reward-induced cognitive effort expenditure. *Cognition*, *172*, 101–106. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cognition.2017.12.004
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Experimental/Intervention, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** Stroop task, task-switching paradigm, Need for Cognition scale, BIS/BAS, Barratt Impulsiveness Scale, GAD-7
- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability, Other
- **Topic:** Motivation/Effort
- **Quality:** N = 45 | Cognitive capacity and NFC predict reward-induced effort; not a personality study.
- **Notes:** N=54 (45 after exclusions). Lower executive function capacity (larger Stroop interference) → greater reward-induced reductions in switch costs. Low NFC also predicted larger reward-driven effort increases. Effects independent of reward sensitivity (BAS).

- **Quality:** Prestige: XL | *Psychological Bulletin*. Neurobehavioral foundation of environmental reactivity.
- **Notes:** Combinatorial framework: [(DA + OP + OXT) : CRH × 1/(5-HT + NE + GABA)]. Maps onto personality traits. Threshold model of reactivity with genetic polymorphisms for each system.

### 173. Waters_etal_2003.pdf

- **Quality:** N = 158 | Attentional bias predicts smoking cessation; not a personality study.

### 177. saunders_2015.pdf

- **Quality:** N = 427,037 (UK Biobank GWAS); 916 (twin validation) | Genetic correlations: L | Largest GWAS of common EF. GABAergic pathway enrichment. cEF genetically separable from IQ (rg = 0.74). European ancestry only. Genetic correlations with psychiatric traits.
- **Notes:** GWAS of common EF (N = 427,037 UK Biobank). 129 significant lead SNPs in 112 loci. SNP h² = 0.10. Associated with GABAergic/synaptic pathways, not dopaminergic. Genetic r with IQ = 0.74 (separable). cEF negatively correlated with most psychiatric disorders; controlling for IQ, cEF remained significant predictor of internalizing and thought disorders.
### 239. horchar_Wohleb_2019.pdf

- **Purpose:** Original Research

- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Other
- **Topic:** Stress / Neuroimmunology
- **Quality:** N = n = 4–8 per group | GR antagonism prevents stress-induced microglial neuronal remodeling and spine loss in mPFC. Preclinical; small per-group N.
- **Notes:** 14-day CUS in mice. RU486 (GR antagonist) prevented CUS-induced behavioral despair, anxiety, and cognitive impairment. ### 241. lam_2025.pdf
- **Citation:** Lam, N. H., Mukherjee, A., Wimmer, R. D., Nassar, M. R., Chen, Z. S., & Halassa, M. M. (2025). Prefrontal transthalamic uncertainty processing drives flexible switching. *Nature*, *637*(8044), 127–136. https://doi.org/10.1038/s41586-024-08180-8

- **Methodology:** Experimental/Intervention
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Other

- **Quality:** N = 9 tree shrews + 2 mice | Prefrontal transthalamic uncertainty processing for cognitive flexibility. Novel tree shrew model. Preclinical.
- **Notes:** Tree shrews and mice. MD thalamus independently represents cueing uncertainty and rule uncertainty. ACC error signals route through MD to trigger PFC reconfiguration (ACC→MD→PFC transthalamic pathway). MD activation sufficient to trigger switching; ACC→PFC direct suppression had no impact. Thalamus demixes cortical signals for hierarchical reasoning under uncertainty.

### 245. mukherjee_2021.pdf

### 246. rhoads_2025.pdf

- **Notes:** N = 220 across 3 pre-registered samples. People integrate self- and other-relevant information into single expected values, updated asymmetrically via 4 types of prediction errors. Self-benefiting biases present. - **Instruments:** EF battery (15 tasks: Inhibition, Switching, WM, Updating), BFI (child), ZKA-PQ Impulsivity, Need for Cognition, Grit, PALS, WJ-III Achievement, WASI-II
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Cognitive Ability, g
- **Topic:** Self-Regulation / Executive Function / Personality / Academics
- **Quality:** N = 1,019 (twins) | Structural: L · Heritability: L · Genetic correlations: L | Texas Twin Project; ages 7.8–15.5. 15 EF tasks + personality + academics. ACE models on latent constructs. Cross-sectional only.
- **Notes:** Texas Twin Project (N=1,019 twins, M age 10.79). EF and personality self-regulation weakly correlated phenotypically but shared genetic variance. Openness personality super-factor incrementally predicted reading beyond EF and cognitive abilities.

### 314. Harden_etal_2017.pdf

### 315. MacKillop_etal_2016.pdf
- **Citation:** MacKillop, J., Weafer, J., Gray, J. C., Oshri, A., Palmer, A., & de Wit, H. (2016). The latent structure of impulsivity: Impulsive choice, impulsive action, and impulsive personality traits. *Psychopharmacology*, *233*(18), 3361–3370. https://doi.org/10.1007/s00213-016-4372-0
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** UPPS-P Impulsive Behavior Scale, BIS-11, Delay Discounting Task (iterative + MCQ), Go/NoGo Task, Stop Signal Task, CPT
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Facet, Cognitive Ability
- **Topic:** Impulsivity / Psychometrics
- **Quality:** N = 1,252 | Structural: L | Large two-site sample (U Chicago + U Georgia) of young adults with low substance use. CFA tested 1-, 2-, 3-, and 4-factor models. Three-factor model (Impulsive Choice, Impulsive Action, Impulsive Personality Traits) fit best. Sensation Seeking excluded — did not load on any factor. Measurement invariance by sex supported. Predominantly European ancestry (84%); restricted substance-use range by design.
- **Notes:** Three latent factors were largely uncorrelated (Choice–Action r = .01; Choice–Traits r = −.10; Action–Traits r = .16). Delay discounting indicators had very high loadings (.86–.94) on Impulsive Choice. UPPS-P and BIS subscales showed structural redundancy (latent r = .995 in 4-factor model). AUDIT associated with Impulsive Choice and IPTs; DUDIT with IPTs only.
### 316. Miller_Gizer_2024.pdf
- **Citation:** Miller, A. P., & Gizer, I. R. (2024). Dual-systems models of the genetic architecture of impulsive personality traits: Neurogenetic evidence of distinct but related factors. *Psychological Medicine*, *54*(8), 1533–1543. https://doi.org/10.1017/S0033291723003367
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Twin/Genetic, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** UPPS-P (GWAS), BIS-11 (GWAS), TCI (GWAS), neuroimaging GWAS (cortical volume, surface area, thickness, subcortical)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Facet
- **Topic:** Impulsivity / Genetics / Neuroimaging
- **Quality:** GWAS summary statistics (N_eff = 11,600–557,900 across indicators) | Structural: M · Genetic correlations: M | GenomicSEM of dual-systems models. SSSC model (sensation seeking–self-control, r_g = .60) fit well; UGSC model (urgency–self-control, r_g = .42 ns) required residual covariances. Neuroimaging genetic correlations partially supported hypotheses (lack of self-control negatively associated with cortical thickness, especially PFC). European-ancestry only; urgency and self-control GWAS underpowered (N_eff ~28K).
- **Notes:** First GenomicSEM test of dual-systems models for impulsive personality traits. Sensation seeking positively genetically correlated with cortical surface area; lack of self-control negatively correlated with cortical thickness (especially PFC, max r_g = −.41). No subcortical associations. Three-factor model (all constructs simultaneously) failed to converge.
### 317. SHARMA_2014.pdf
- **Citation:** Sharma, L., Markon, K. E., & Clark, L. A. (2014). Toward a theory of distinct types of "impulsive" behaviors: A meta-analysis of self-report and behavioral measures. *Psychological Bulletin*, *140*(2), 374–408. https://doi.org/10.1037/a0034418
- **Purpose:** Meta-Analysis
- **Methodology:** Meta-Analysis, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** Multiple (58 self-report scales; 15 behavioral tasks — see Tables 1, 4–5)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet, Cognitive Ability
- **Topic:** Impulsivity / Psychometrics
- **Quality:** Prestige: XL · Structural: XL | *Psychological Bulletin*. Three integrated meta-analytic studies. Study 1: 58 × 58 meta-analytic correlation matrix of self-report impulsivity scales → 3 factors (E/PE, DvC/C, N/NE). Study 2: 15 × 15 matrix of lab tasks → 4 factors (Inattention, Inhibition, Impulsive Decision-Making, Shifting). Study 3: Relations of both with daily-life impulsive behaviors. Comprehensive scope; composite ML imputation for missing correlations; predominantly undergraduate samples (84%).
- **Notes:** Self-report impulsivity maps onto three higher-order personality traits: Extraversion/Positive Emotionality (sensation seeking anchors), Disinhibition vs. Constraint/Conscientiousness (with subfactors DvC and C/WvR), and Neuroticism/Negative Emotionality (urgency anchors). Lab tasks form four largely independent factors. Self-report–task correlations consistently low (grand mean r = .02); both independently predict daily-life impulsive behaviors. Joint use offers incremental validity.
### 318. Bavelas_2000.pdf
- **Citation:** Bavelas, J. B., Coates, L., & Johnson, T. (2000). Listeners as co-narrators. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*, *79*(6), 941–952. https://doi.org/10.1037/0022-3514.79.6.941
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Experimental/Intervention
- **Instruments:** Custom behavioral coding system for listener responses
- **Level of Detail:** Other (communication / conversational behavior)
- **Topic:** Social Cognition / Interpersonal Communication
- **Quality:** N = 86 + 68 (2 experiments) | Structural: M | Novel coding system with adequate reliability; small sample sizes; student-only participants. Single sociocultural context.
- **Notes:** Two experiments on face-to-face storytelling dyads. Distinguishes generic (audience) from specific (co-narrator) listener responses. Distracted listeners produce fewer specific responses; narrators told to distracted listeners produce lower-quality stories. Listeners are active co-narrators.
### 319. Brunell_etal_2008.pdf
- **Citation:** Brunell, A. B., Gentry, W. A., Campbell, W. K., Hoffman, B. J., Kuhnert, K. W., & DeMarree, K. G. (2008). Leader emergence: The case of the narcissistic leader. *Personality and Social Psychology Bulletin*, *34*(12), 1663–1676. https://doi.org/10.1177/0146167208324101
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Experimental/Intervention
- **Instruments:** NPI, BFI, CPI narcissism scale, Rosenberg Self-Esteem Inventory
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Other (narcissism dimensions)
- **Topic:** Narcissism / Leadership
- **Quality:** N = 432 + 408 + 153 (3 studies) | Structural: L | Multi-method (peer, self, expert ratings) across student and executive samples. Self-report only for predictors; cross-sectional.
- **Notes:** Narcissism (especially NPI power dimension) predicts leader emergence in leaderless group discussions across three studies, but not task performance. Effect holds after controlling for Big Five and self-esteem.
### 320. Campbell_2004.pdf
- **Citation:** Campbell, W. K., Bonacci, A. M., Shelton, J., Exline, J. J., & Bushman, B. J. (2004). Psychological entitlement: Interpersonal consequences and validation of a self-report measure. *Journal of Personality Assessment*, *83*(1), 29–45. https://doi.org/10.1207/s15327752jpa8301_04
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis, Instrument Validation, Experimental/Intervention
- **Instruments:** Psychological Entitlement Scale (PES, 9-item, new), NPI, BFI, Rosenberg Self-Esteem Inventory, BIDR
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Other (entitlement)
- **Topic:** Narcissism / Psychometrics
- **Quality:** Total N > 2,750 (9 studies) | Structural: XL | CFA, test-retest (.70–.72), discriminant validity from NPI Entitlement, convergent/criterion validity with behavioral outcomes. All undergraduate samples.
- **Notes:** 9-item single-factor PES (α = .85–.88). Distinct from NPI Entitlement (r = .64 latent). Predicts selfish behavior, aggression after ego threat, poor relationship functioning. Not redundant with Big Five.
### 321. Chotai_Wiseman_2005.pdf
- **Citation:** Chotai, J., & Wiseman, R. (2005). Born lucky? The relationship between feeling lucky and month of birth. *Personality and Individual Differences*, *39*(8), 1451–1460. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.paid.2005.06.012
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** Custom 13-item luck/personality survey
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Other (luck beliefs, season of birth)
- **Topic:** Personality / Developmental Neuroscience
- **Quality:** N = 29,584 | Developmental: M | Massive N but Internet self-selection, non-validated instrument, cross-sectional only. Non-standard instrument with unknown psychometrics.
- **Notes:** Summer-born UK participants feel luckier (peak May, nadir November). Luck beliefs correlate with lower N, higher O, higher E — all showing the same seasonal pattern. Attributable fraction ~3.4%, comparable to single gene-allele effects.
### 322. Colman_2006.pdf
- **Citation:** Colman, D. R. (2006). The three princes of Serendip: Notes on a mysterious phenomenon. *McGill Journal of Medicine*, *9*(2), 161–163.
- **Purpose:** Commentary/Editorial
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Other (history of science)
- **Topic:** Serendipity / History of Science
- **Quality:** Prestige: S | Short essay in a student-run medical journal. Historical anecdotes of serendipitous discoveries (penicillin, X-rays, Cajal/Golgi).
- **Notes:** Reviews famous examples of serendipity in science. Emphasizes Pasteur's "prepared mind." No empirical or theoretical framework.
### 323. Copeland_2019.pdf
- **Citation:** Copeland, S. (2019). On serendipity in science: Discovery at the intersection of chance and wisdom. *Synthese*, *196*(6), 2385–2406. https://doi.org/10.1007/s11229-017-1544-3
- **Purpose:** Review
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Other (philosophy of science / epistemology)
- **Topic:** Serendipity / Philosophy of Science
- **Quality:** Prestige: L | *Synthese*. Rigorous philosophical analysis drawing on case studies and empirical interview research.
- **Notes:** Serendipity as emergent property of discovery: involves disruption of epistemic expectations, is retrospectively identified, and occurs at community level. Supports early publication and broad credit in science.
### 324. DeMarree_2018.pdf
- **Citation:** DeMarree, K. G., & Bobrowski, M. E. (2018). Structure and validity of self-concept clarity measures. In J. Lodi-Smith & K. G. DeMarree (Eds.), *Self-concept clarity: Perspectives on assessment, research, and applications* (pp. 1–17). Springer. https://doi.org/10.1007/978-3-319-71547-6_1
- **Purpose:** Book Chapter
- **Methodology:** Factor Analysis, Instrument Validation, Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** SCCS, Rosenberg Self-Esteem Scale, CES-D, satisfaction with life scale
- **Level of Detail:** Other (self-concept clarity measurement)
- **Topic:** Psychometrics / Self-Concept
- **Quality:** N = 347 + confirmatory sample | Structural: L · Prestige: L | Opening chapter in Springer edited volume. ESEM reveals three SCC factors, not one. Undergraduate samples; self-report only.
- **Notes:** Six SCC measurement strategies do not converge (median inter-r = .09). ESEM yields three factors: SCCS, certainty/extremity, latitudes. Many SCC effects eliminated after controlling self-esteem. Recommends specifying which SCC feature is measured.
### 325. DeMarree_2023.pdf
- **Citation:** DeMarree, K. G., Chang, Y.-H., Lee, T., & Venezia, A. (2023). Listening and attitude change. *Current Opinion in Psychology*, *53*, 101641. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.copsyc.2023.101641
- **Purpose:** Review
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Other (attitude change, listening behavior)
- **Topic:** Social Cognition / Attitude Change
- **Quality:** Prestige: M | *Current Opinion in Psychology*. Review of emerging research on listening quality and attitude change.
- **Notes:** High-quality listening reduces anxiety, increases psychological safety, promotes open-minded self-reflection. Speakers report less extreme attitudes, greater ambivalence, greater clarity. Listening in canvassing durably reduces prejudice.
### 326. Dumas_2026.pdf
- **Citation:** Dumas, D., & Campbell, W. K. (2026). Exploring the creative personality: Using machine learning to predict fluency and originality in divergent thinking. *Creativity Research Journal*. Advance online publication. https://doi.org/10.1080/10400419.2024.2371725
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** BFAS, Alternate Uses Task (AUT), Open Creativity Scoring
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Aspect, Item-Level
- **Topic:** Personality / Creativity
- **Quality:** N = 334 | Structural: M | LASSO regression on BFAS items predicting DT. Single sample, no out-of-sample replication. Single sociocultural context.
- **Notes:** Enthusiasm (E) and low Withdrawal (N) best predict fluency — not Openness. Openness items best predict originality. Industriousness/Orderliness negatively associated with both. Fluency and originality have distinct personality profiles.
### 327. Dumas_Dunbar_2014.pdf
- **Citation:** Dumas, D., & Dunbar, K. N. (2016). The creative stereotype effect. *PLoS ONE*, *11*(2), e0142567. https://doi.org/10.1371/journal.pone.0142567

- **Level of Detail:** Other (creative cognition / stereotypes)
- **Topic:** Creativity / Social Cognition
- **Quality:** N = 96 + 91 (2 studies) | Prestige: M | PLoS ONE. Moderate-to-large effect sizes. Student samples only.
- **Notes:** Adopting an "eccentric poet" stereotype enhances originality (but not fluency) on the AUT vs. "rigid librarian" or control. Replicates within-subjects. LSA-based scoring validated.
### 328. Erdelez_2000.pdf
- **Citation:** Erdelez, S. (2000). Towards understanding information encountering on the Web. *Proceedings of the 63rd Annual Meeting of the American Society for Information Science*, *37*, 363–371.
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** Custom survey instrument
- **Level of Detail:** Other (information behavior)
- **Topic:** Information Behavior / Serendipity
- **Quality:** N = 137 | Structural: S | Exploratory survey, convenience sample, no validated instrument.
- **Notes:** Information encountering (IE) is common on the Web. Users range from "super-encounterers" to "non-encounterers." Super-encounterers modify their environment to facilitate accidental discovery.
### 329. Erdelez_2005.pdf
- **Citation:** Erdelez, S. (2005). Information encountering. In K. E. Fisher, S. Erdelez, & L. McKechnie (Eds.), *Theories of information behavior* (pp. 179–184). Information Today.

- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Other (information behavior theory)
- **Topic:** Information Behavior / Serendipity
- **Quality:** Prestige: M | Chapter in a well-regarded information science reference volume.
- **Notes:** Theoretical overview of IE framework. Five stages: noticing, stopping, examining, capturing, returning. Individual differences in IE propensity. Distinct from serendipity, browsing, incidental acquisition.
### 330. Heinström_2003.pdf
- **Citation:** Heinström, J. (2003). Five personality dimensions and their influence on information behaviour. *Information Research*, *9*(1), paper 165.
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** NEO-FFI, custom information behavior questionnaire
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain
- **Topic:** Personality / Information Behavior
- **Quality:** N = 305 | Structural: M | Standard personality instrument (NEO-FFI). Domain-level only; single sociocultural context (Finnish students). Non-validated information behavior measure.
- **Notes:** Openness strongest predictor of deep, exploratory information seeking and incidental discovery. Three patterns: "fast surfing" (high N, low O, low C), "broad scanning" (high E, high O), "deep diving" (high C, high O).
### 331. Heinström_2006.pdf
- **Citation:** Heinström, J. (2006). Fast surfing for availability or deep diving into quality — motivation and information seeking among middle and high school students. *Information Research*, *11*(4), paper 265.
- **Purpose:** Original Research

- **Instruments:** Achievement Goal Questionnaire, Study Process Questionnaire (SPQ), custom information-seeking questionnaire
- **Level of Detail:** Other (motivation / information behavior)
- **Topic:** Information Behavior
- **Quality:** N = 574 | Structural: M | Adequate N. No validated personality measures; non-standard information behavior measure. Single sociocultural context.
- **Notes:** Extends fast surfing / deep diving distinction to secondary school students. Mastery goals predict deep diving; performance-avoidance predicts fast surfing. Study approach mediates motivation–information seeking link.
### 332. Kernis_Goldman_2006.pdf
- **Citation:** Kernis, M. H., & Goldman, B. M. (2006). A multicomponent conceptualization of authenticity: Theory and research. *Advances in Experimental Social Psychology*, *38*, 283–357. https://doi.org/10.1016/S0065-2601(06)38006-9
- **Purpose:** Review
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review, Factor Analysis, Instrument Validation, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** Authenticity Inventory (AI-3, 45-item), NEO-FFI, MAAS, KIMS, DVBA, Ryff PWB Scale, multiple self-esteem measures
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Facet, Personality Domain
- **Topic:** Personality / Authenticity / Self-Concept
- **Quality:** CFA N = 294 + multiple validation samples | Structural: L · Prestige: XL | *Advances in Experimental Social Psychology*. CFA confirms four-component hierarchical model. Behavioral validation via DVBA. Self-report only for most analyses; single university.
- **Notes:** Authenticity = awareness + unbiased processing + behavioral authenticity + relational orientation. CFA supports hierarchical model. Authenticity predicts lower verbal defensiveness, higher mindfulness, adaptive coping, well-being, relationship satisfaction. Parental authoritativeness predicts adult authenticity.
### 333. Kluger_2022.pdf
- **Citation:** Kluger, A. N., & Itzchakov, G. (2022). The power of listening at work. *Annual Review of Organizational Psychology and Organizational Behavior*, *9*, 121–146. https://doi.org/10.1146/annurev-orgpsych-012420-091013

- **Topic:** Social Cognition / Organizational Psychology
- **Quality:** Prestige: XL | *Annual Review of Organizational Psychology and Organizational Behavior*.
- **Notes:** Listening encompasses attention, comprehension, and intention. Associated with job performance (r = .38–.47), leadership (r = .50–.70), trust, well-being. Proposes "episodic listening theory" — listening creates dyadic episodes of "togetherness." About half of listening perception variance is dyad-level.
### 334. Maltby_2008.pdf
- **Citation:** Maltby, J., Day, L., Gill, P., Colley, A., & Wood, A. M. (2008). Beliefs around luck: Confirming the empirical conceptualization of beliefs around luck and the development of the Darke and Freedman beliefs around luck scale. *Personality and Individual Differences*, *45*(7), 655–660. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.paid.2008.07.010

- **Notes:** Confirms Darke & Freedman scale factor structure. Luck belief correlates with irrationality and paranormal beliefs. Distinct from locus of control. Scale conflates belief in luck as force vs. personal luckiness.
### 335. Miller_2011.pdf
- **Citation:** Miller, J. D., Hoffman, B. J., Gaughan, E. T., Gentile, B., Maples, J., & Campbell, W. K. (2011). Grandiose and vulnerable narcissism: A nomological network analysis. *Journal of Personality*, *79*(5), 1013–1042. https://doi.org/10.1111/j.1467-6494.2010.00711.x
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis

- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Topic:** Narcissism / Personality
- **Quality:** N = 490 (+ 194 with informant data) | Structural: L | Multi-method (self-report, informant, behavioral, thin-slice ratings). Single sociocultural context (U.S. undergraduates).
- **Notes:** Grandiose and vulnerable narcissism have strikingly different nomological networks. Grandiose: low A, high E, low N. Vulnerable: high N, low A, low E. Both share entitlement and aggression. PNI grandiose scales loaded more on vulnerable factor.
### 336. Miwa_2025.pdf
- **Citation:** Miwa, K., Yamashita, W., & Morita, S. (2025). Luck cognition in daily life: Effects of perceived control, positive cognitive bias, and affective experience on life satisfaction. *Scientific Reports*, *15*, 18744. https://doi.org/10.1038/s41598-025-95457-1

- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis

- **Level of Detail:** Other (luck cognition, life satisfaction)
- **Topic:** Heuristics & Biases / Social Cognition
- **Quality:** N = 516 + 300 (2 studies) | Structural: M | Adequate N, new non-standard instrument, single sociocultural context (Japan).
- **Notes:** Three distinct luck cognition components: perceived control, positive cognitive bias, affective experience. All three predict life satisfaction independently. Extends Thompson & Prendergast's bidimensional model to three dimensions.
### 337. Naragon-Gainey_2017.pdf
- **Citation:** Naragon-Gainey, K., & DeMarree, K. G. (2017). Structure and validity of measures of decentering and defusion. *Psychological Assessment*, *29*(7), 935–954. https://doi.org/10.1037/pas0000405
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis, Instrument Validation
- **Instruments:** EQ, TMS-D, CFQ, DDS, BAFT, BFI, PANAS, Rosenberg Self-Esteem Scale, PTQ, RRS-B, MEAQ, SCCS, ERQ, IDAS
