- **Quality:** N = 351 + 344 + 503 + 211 (4 samples) | Structural: L | Multi-sample with ESEM + CFA cross-validation; clinical and non-clinical samples. Self-report only.
- **Notes:** Decentering/defusion measures converge weakly (mean r = .29–.47). Two factors: Observer Perspective (OP) and Reduced Struggle (RS). RS nearly indistinguishable from neuroticism. Negative item valence confounds measurement — 80% of items reference negative experiences.
### 338. Paredes_etal_2026.pdf
- **Citation:** Paredes, B., Brinol, P., Santos, D., Moreno, L., Guyer, J. J., & Petty, R. E. (2026). Attitudes guiding social behavior as a function of perceived knowledge: The moderating role of epistemic vs. hedonic mindsets. *Journal of Experimental Social Psychology*, *123*, 104857. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.jesp.2025.104857
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Experimental/Intervention
- **Instruments:** Custom attitude scales, behavioral intention scales, perceived knowledge measures
- **Level of Detail:** Other (attitudes, attitude-behavior correspondence)
- **Topic:** Social Cognition / Attitudes
- **Quality:** N = 262 + 248 + 337 + 356 (4 studies + 4 supplementary) | Prestige: L | *JESP*. Multi-study with pre-registration (Study 3). Small-to-medium effects.
- **Notes:** Perceived knowledge enhances attitude-behavior correspondence under epistemic mindset but reverses it under hedonic mindset. First demonstration of full reversal of the knowledge effect. Mechanism: mindset changes meaning of knowledge.
### 339. Petty_2007.pdf
- **Citation:** Petty, R. E., Brinol, P., & DeMarree, K. G. (2007). The Meta-Cognitive Model (MCM) of attitudes: Implications for attitude measurement, change, and strength. *Social Cognition*, *25*(5), 657–686. https://doi.org/10.1521/soco.2007.25.5.657
- **Purpose:** Review
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Other (attitudes, metacognition)
- **Topic:** Social Cognition / Attitudes
- **Quality:** Prestige: L | *Social Cognition*. Major theoretical contribution from leading attitude researchers.
- **Notes:** MCM: attitude objects linked to positive/negative evaluative associations, each tagged with validity meta-cognitions (true/false). Single integrated representation, not dual stores. Explains automatic-deliberative discrepancies, implicit ambivalence, sleeper effect, and prejudice via negation tags.
### 340. Thompson_2013.html
- **Citation:** Thompson, E. R., & Prendergast, G. P. (2013). Belief in luck and luckiness: Conceptual clarification and new measure validation. *Personality and Individual Differences*, *54*(4), 501–506. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.paid.2012.10.027
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis, Instrument Validation
- **Instruments:** Belief in Luck and Luckiness Scale (12-item, new), Darke and Freedman Belief in Good Luck Scale, NEO-FFI
- **Level of Detail:** Other (luck beliefs)
- **Topic:** Psychometrics / Personality
- **Quality:** Total N = 1,205 (multiple samples) | Structural: L | Multi-sample CFA, cross-cultural samples. Single primary context for initial validation (Hong Kong/Asian).
- **Notes:** Luck beliefs are bidimensional: Belief in Luck (BiL, linked to irrationality/Neuroticism) vs. Belief in Personal Luckiness (BPL, linked to positive affect/wellbeing). Uncorrelated dimensions. Existing unidimensional scales conflate these.
### 341. Thompson_2019.pdf
- **Citation:** Thompson, E. R., Prendergast, G. P., & Dericks, G. H. (2019). Personality, luck beliefs, and (non-?) problem lottery gambling. *Applied Research in Quality of Life*, *16*, 703–722. https://doi.org/10.1007/s11482-019-09791-4
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** International English Big-Five Mini-Markers, Belief in Luck and Luckiness Scale, lottery gambling frequency measure
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain
- **Topic:** Personality / Heuristics & Biases
- **Quality:** N = 844 | Structural: M | Domain-level only (8 items per domain). Single sociocultural context (Hong Kong).
- **Notes:** Belief in Luck is strongest predictor of lottery gambling (β = .51). Big Five also predict: E (+), N (+), O (−), A (−). Luck beliefs predict gambling independently of Big Five. State-sponsored lotteries may share psychological determinants with problem gambling.
### 342. Thompson_2022.pdf
- **Citation:** Thompson, E. R., & Prendergast, G. P. (2022). Belief in luck and luckiness: Conceptual clarification, new measure validation, and their relationship with happiness and the five-factor personality model. *Current Psychology*, *41*, 29–40. https://doi.org/10.1007/s12144-019-00535-1
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** Belief in Luck and Luckiness Scale, Subjective Happiness Scale, I-PANAS-SF, LOT-R, International English Big-Five Mini-Markers
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Other (luck beliefs, happiness)
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** N = 844 | Structural: M | Domain-level Big Five (8 items per domain). Single sociocultural context (Hong Kong).
- **Notes:** Belief in Luck negatively associated with happiness, fully mediated by Neuroticism. Belief in Personal Luckiness positively associated with happiness and shares unique variance beyond Big Five. Luckiness may be a discrete trait not captured by the FFM.
### 343. Trapnell_1999.pdf
- **Citation:** Trapnell, P. D., & Campbell, J. D. (1999). Private self-consciousness and the five-factor model of personality: Distinguishing rumination from reflection. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology*, *76*(2), 284–304. https://doi.org/10.1037/0022-3514.76.2.284
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis, Instrument Validation
- **Instruments:** Self-Consciousness Scales (SCS), Rumination-Reflection Questionnaire (RRQ, 24-item, new), NEO-FFI, NEO-PI-R, IASR-B5, Rosenberg Self-Esteem Scale, PANAS, BDI, Need for Cognition Scale
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet, Item-Level
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** Total N ≈ 3,500+ (multiple samples) | Structural: L | Multiple independent samples with different Big Five instruments, cross-validation. Self-report only; North American students.
- **Notes:** Private Self-Consciousness confounds rumination (neurotic self-focus, r = .57–.64 with N) and reflection (epistemic self-focus, r = .61–.68 with O). RRQ (α > .90) separates these. Resolves the "self-absorption paradox": distress comes from rumination, self-knowledge from reflection.
### 344. Twenge_2008.pdf
- **Citation:** Twenge, J. M., Konrath, S., Foster, J. D., Campbell, W. K., & Bushman, B. J. (2008). Egos inflating over time: A cross-temporal meta-analysis of the Narcissistic Personality Inventory. *Journal of Personality*, *76*(4), 875–901. https://doi.org/10.1111/j.1467-6494.2008.00507.x
- **Purpose:** Meta-Analysis
- **Methodology:** Meta-Analysis, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** NPI (40-item)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Other (narcissism total score)
- **Topic:** Narcissism
- **Quality:** 85 samples, N = 16,475 | Developmental: L | 27-year span (1979–2006). Consistent instrument across all data points. Cannot separate cohort from period effects. Domain-level only; self-report; U.S. college students only.
- **Notes:** NPI scores increased ~0.33 SD from early 1980s to 2006 (β = .53). Two-thirds of 2006 students above 1979–1985 mean. Increase driven primarily by women; sex difference narrowed from d = .45 to d = .15.
### 345. Twenge_2025.pdf
- **Citation:** Twenge, J. M. (2025). Technology and cultural change. In D. T. Gilbert, S. T. Fiske, E. J. Finkel, & W. B. Mendes (Eds.), *The handbook of social psychology* (6th ed.). Situational Press. https://doi.org/10.70400/BZNV4498
- **Purpose:** Book Chapter
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Other (cultural change, generational differences)
- **Topic:** Personality / Cultural Change
- **Quality:** Prestige: XL | *Handbook of Social Psychology* (6th ed.). Flagship reference.
- **Notes:** "Technology Model of Cultural Change" — technology drives cohort differences via individualism and slow life strategy. Narcissism (NPI) showed curvilinear trend: rising to ~2008, declining post-recession. Smartphones/social media linked to adolescent depression surge since early 2010s.
### 346. Wiseman_2002.pdf
- **Citation:** Wiseman, R. (2003). The luck factor. *The Skeptical Inquirer*, *27*(3), 26–30.
- **Purpose:** Commentary/Editorial
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** LOT-R (referenced informally)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Other (luck-related behaviors)
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** Prestige: S | Popular magazine article (The Skeptical Inquirer). Not peer-reviewed. Informal reporting without statistics.
- **Notes:** Lucky people: higher E (larger networks), higher O (receptive to novelty), lower N/anxiety (less attentional narrowing). "Luck school" intervention increased self-reported luck and satisfaction. Luck = behaviors and attitudes, not magical ability.
### 347. Womick_2019.pdf
- **Citation:** Womick, J., Foltz, R. M., & King, L. A. (2019). "Releasing the beast within"? Authenticity, well-being, and the Dark Tetrad. *Personality and Individual Differences*, *137*, 115–125. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.paid.2018.08.022
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** Authenticity Inventory (AI-3), Short Dark Triad (SD3), NPI, Mach IV, LSRP, ASP, MLQ-P, SWLS, BIDR
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Other (Dark Tetrad, authenticity)
- **Topic:** Personality / Dark Traits
- **Quality:** N = 404 + 415 (2 studies) | Structural: M | Two MTurk samples with adequate Ns. Cross-sectional; MTurk convenience samples; self-report only.
- **Notes:** Dark Tetrad moderates the authenticity–well-being link: among those high on dark traits, authenticity is less strongly related to well-being. At low authenticity, dark traits are associated with higher well-being. "Being true to oneself" may not universally promote well-being.
### 348. Young_2009.pdf
- **Citation:** Young, M. J., Chen, N., & Morris, M. W. (2009). Belief in stable and fleeting luck and achievement motivation. *Personality and Individual Differences*, *47*(2), 150–154. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.paid.2009.02.009
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Experimental/Intervention
- **Instruments:** Belief in Luck Scale (BIL), ad hoc Belief in Fleeting Luck subscale (new), Big Five (brief), Need for Achievement scale, Achievement Goal Questionnaire
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Other (luck beliefs, achievement motivation)
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** N = 78 + 74 (2 studies) | Structural: S | Small samples; novel unvalidated construct (fleeting luck). Single sociocultural context.
- **Notes:** Stable luck belief → higher achievement motivation, correlated with E. Fleeting luck belief → lower achievement motivation, correlated with N. After success, fleeting-luck believers increase effort; after failure, they decrease effort. Two distinct motivational profiles.
### 349. Allport_Odbert_1936.pdf
- **Citation:** Allport, G. W., & Odbert, H. S. (1936). Trait-names: A psycho-lexical study. *Psychological Monographs, 47*(1, Whole No. 211), 1–171. https://doi.org/10.1037/h0093360
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Systematic Review (lexical enumeration)
- **Instruments:** Webster's New International Dictionary (1925 edition)
- **Level of Detail:** Item-Level
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** Prestige: XL | Foundational monograph launching the lexical tradition. *Psychological Monographs*.
- **Notes:** Catalogued 17,953 English person-descriptive terms from the unabridged dictionary into four columns (personal traits, temporary states, social evaluations, miscellaneous). Starting point for all subsequent psycholexical research.
### 350. CHRISTENSEN_2020.pdf
- **Citation:** Christensen, A. P., Golino, H. F., & Silvia, P. J. (2020). A psychometric network perspective on the validity and validation of personality trait questionnaires. *European Journal of Personality, 34*(6), 1095–1108. https://doi.org/10.1002/per.2265
- **Purpose:** Review
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A (discusses NEO-PI-R, BFI, HEXACO conceptually)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet, Item-Level
- **Topic:** Psychometrics
- **Quality:** Prestige: L | *European Journal of Personality*. Network psychometrics framework for personality validity.
- **Notes:** Proposes psychometric network framework for validating personality questionnaires. Introduces structural consistency (via bootEGA) and network loadings as network equivalents of factor-analytic concepts.
### 351. condon_etal_2021.pdf
- **Citation:** Condon, D. M., Wood, D., Mottus, R., Booth, T., Costantini, G., Greiff, S., Johnson, W., Lukaszewski, A., Murray, A., Revelle, W., Wright, A. G. C., Ziegler, M., & Zimmermann, J. (2020). Bottom up construction of a personality taxonomy. *European Journal of Psychological Assessment, 36*(6), 923–934. https://doi.org/10.1027/1015-5759/a000626
- **Purpose:** Commentary/Editorial
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A (discusses IPIP, NEO-PI-R, HEXACO, BFI-2 conceptually)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Facet, Item-Level
- **Topic:** Personality, Psychometrics
- **Quality:** Prestige: L | *European Journal of Psychological Assessment*. Invited article from expert meeting.
- **Notes:** Proposes 6-step bottom-up procedure for building personality taxonomy from item-level nuances. Argues existing hierarchies suffer from jingle/jangle problems and incomplete coverage below domain level.
### 352. Cutler_Condon_2022.pdf
- **Citation:** Cutler, A., & Condon, D. M. (2022). Deep lexical hypothesis: Identifying personality structure in natural language. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology, 123*(4), 877–899. https://doi.org/10.1037/pspp0000443
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Factor Analysis, Cross-Sectional
- **Instruments:** DeBERTa language model, Saucier & Goldberg (1996) 435-adjective set, Allport & Odbert 17,913-term set
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Item-Level
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** Structural: L | Three studies with multiple adjective sets and language models. First 3 components (A, E, C) well-recovered; N and O/I not. Novel NLP methodology.
- **Notes:** Uses transformer language models to extract personality structure from adjective semantics without human ratings. First 3 unrotated components highly congruent with survey data (.79–.89); N and O/I poorly recovered. Supports a "Big Three" from NLP.
### 353. De Raad_etal_2010.pdf
- **Citation:** De Raad, B., Barelds, D. P. H., Levert, E., Ostendorf, F., Mlačić, B., Di Blas, L., Hřebíčková, M., Szirmák, Z., Szarota, P., Perugini, M., Church, A. T., & Katigbak, M. S. (2010). Only three factors of personality description are fully replicable across languages: A comparison of 14 trait taxonomies. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology, 98*(1), 160–173. https://doi.org/10.1037/a0017184
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Factor Analysis, Mega-Analysis
- **Instruments:** 14 psycholexical trait taxonomies from 12 languages
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** Structural: XL | 14 independent datasets across 12 languages, 91 pairwise comparisons. Domain-level only.
- **Notes:** Only E, A, C replicate with congruence ≥ .80 across all 14 languages. Emotional Stability, Intellect, and Honesty-Humility do not consistently replicate. Supports a "Big Three" as the cross-culturally replicable core.
### 354. Golino_2025.pdf
- **Citation:** Golino, H. F., Nesselroade, J. R., & Christensen, A. P. (2025). The ergodicity information index: A new metric for quantifying the information loss when representing a set of within-person structures as a single between-person structure. *Psychological Methods*. Advance online publication. https://doi.org/10.1037/met0000716
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Experience Sampling, Factor Analysis, Mega-Analysis
- **Instruments:** DynEGA (Dynamic Exploratory Graph Analysis), EGAnet R package
- **Level of Detail:** Item-Level, Personality Domain, Other (network structure)
- **Topic:** Psychometrics
- **Quality:** Structural: L | Novel metric with Monte Carlo validation (216 conditions, 500 replications). 83.5% accuracy (unweighted). Performance degrades with high measurement error.
- **Notes:** Introduces the Ergodicity Information Index (EII) quantifying information lost when representing within-person structures as a single between-person structure. Uses Kolmogorov complexity of network encodings. Major contribution to idiographic vs. nomothetic debate.
### 355. Granziol_Cona_2024.pdf
- **Citation:** Granziol, U., & Cona, G. (2024). Architecture and relationships among cognition, mental health and other human domains revealed by network analysis perspective. *Current Psychology, 43*, 4945–4960. https://doi.org/10.1007/s12144-023-04698-8
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** HCP database: NEO-FFI, NIH Toolbox Cognition Battery, ASR, Delay Discounting, AUDIT
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Cognitive Ability, Other (mental health, substance use)
- **Topic:** Neuroscience
- **Quality:** N = 1,206 | Structural: L | Large HCP sample, EGA with cross-validation (CFI = .943). Bayesian Network adds directed pathways. Cross-sectional; NEO-FFI domain-level only.
- **Notes:** Seven interrelated domains: Mental Health, Externalizing, High Cognitive Functions, Basic Cognitive Functions, Substance Use, Delay Discounting, Pain. Crystallized intelligence most central node. Cognitive functions cluster into two domains.
### 356. Henry_Mottus_2025.pdf
- **Citation:** Henry, S., & Mõttus, R. (2025). 100 Nuances of Personality. *European Journal of Personality*. Advance online publication. https://doi.org/10.1177/08902070251314211
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Instrument Validation, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** 100 Nuances of Personality (100NP; 198 items), SAPA, IPIP, HEXACO-PI-R
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Facet, Item-Level
- **Topic:** Personality, Psychometrics
- **Quality:** N = 858 (dev) + 77,000+ (Estonian Biobank) | Structural: L | Iterative development over 5 versions, multiple validity criteria. Single English-language derivation.
- **Notes:** 198-item pool (100NP) maximizing bandwidth, reliability, and non-redundancy at nuance level. Median r_tt = .69, median r_ca = .37. Deployed in Estonian Biobank (N > 77,000) and Generation Scotland.
### 357. ICD-11 Personality Disorders.pdf
- **Citation:** Mulder, R. T. (2021). ICD-11 personality disorders: Utility and implications of the new model. *Frontiers in Psychiatry, 12*, Article 655548. https://doi.org/10.3389/fpsyt.2021.655548
- **Purpose:** Review
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** ICD-11 PD classification, PiCD, PID-5, DSM-5 AMPD
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Other (personality pathology)
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** Prestige: M | *Frontiers in Psychiatry*. Mini-review by ICD-11 PD Classification Committee member.
- **Notes:** ICD-11 abolishes categorical PD types for severity dimension (mild/moderate/severe) plus 5 trait qualifiers (negative affectivity, detachment, dissociality, disinhibition, anankastia). Aligns with DSM-5 AMPD.
### 358. Menardi_etal_2026.pdf
- **Citation:** Menardi, A., Ozer, Z. G., Vallesi, A., Cona, G., & Granziol, U. (2026). Linking individual behavioral architecture to brain topological structure: A combined network analysis approach. *Biological Psychology, 205*, Article 109235. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.biopsycho.2026.109235
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** HCP behavioral battery, NEO-FFI, resting-state fMRI (Schaefer atlas, 7 RSNs)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Cognitive Ability, Other (brain network topology)
- **Topic:** Neuroscience
- **Quality:** N = 379 | Structural: M | HCP sample, EGA + GAMs, multiple threshold checks. Moderate N for brain-behavior associations; cross-sectional; domain-level personality only.
- **Notes:** Between-network connectivity (FPN modularity, DMN/LIMB participation) more predictive of cognitive-behavioral differences than within-network properties. Supports distributed brain-behavior models.
### 359. Michelini_etal_2024.pdf
- **Citation:** Michelini, G., Carlisi, C. O., Eaton, N. R., Elison, J. T., Haltigan, J. D., Kotov, R., Krueger, R. F., Latzman, R. D., Li, J. J., Levin-Aspenson, H. F., Salum, G. A., South, S. C., Stanton, K., Waldman, I. D., & Wilson, S. (2024). Where do neurodevelopmental conditions fit in transdiagnostic psychiatric frameworks? Incorporating a new neurodevelopmental spectrum. *World Psychiatry, 23*(3), 333–357. https://doi.org/10.1002/wps.21225
- **Purpose:** Review
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review, Systematic Review
- **Instruments:** References CBCL, ASEBA, PID-5, SRS, ASRS, various ASD/ADHD measures
- **Level of Detail:** Other (transdiagnostic spectra: neurodevelopmental, internalizing, externalizing)
- **Topic:** Psychometrics, Neuroscience
- **Quality:** Prestige: XL | *World Psychiatry* (IF ~60). Massive scope (405 references), multi-author expert team.
- **Notes:** Proposes formal inclusion of a "neurodevelopmental spectrum" (ADHD, ASD, learning/motor/communication disorders) into transdiagnostic frameworks like HiTOP. Reviews structural, genetic, neurobiological, cognitive, and clinical utility evidence.
### 360. Michelini_etal_2025.pdf
- **Citation:** Michelini, G., Liao, W., Lu, S., Caserini, C., Eley, T. C., Ronald, A., Wilson, S., Malanchini, M., & Rimfeld, K. (2025). The neurodevelopmental spectrum: Phenotypic architecture, etiology, and predictive utility across development. *medRxiv*. https://doi.org/10.1101/2025.07.31.25332492
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Longitudinal, Twin/Genetic, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** TEDS battery (parent/self-reported neurodevelopmental items), polygenic scores (ADHD, autism, Tourette), cognitive measures (g, reading, exams)
- **Level of Detail:** Other (neurodevelopmental spectrum factor), Cognitive Ability, g
- **Topic:** Psychometrics, Neuroscience
- **Quality:** N = 10,261–15,668 per wave | Structural: XL · Heritability: XL · Genetic correlations: L | Very large TEDS twin sample, 3 developmental waves, pre-registered. Preprint / not peer-reviewed. Parent-report primary.
- **Notes:** Neurodevelopmental spectrum factor (ADHD + autistic traits + learning/motor difficulties) at ages 7, 12, 16. Highly heritable (h² = .60–.82), moderately stable, predicted by neurodevelopmental PGS, predicts cognitive/educational outcomes (R² up to 21%).
### 361. Ringwald_2022.pdf
- **Citation:** Ringwald, W. R., Manuck, S. B., Marsland, A. L., & Wright, A. G. C. (2022). Psychometric evaluation of a Big Five personality state scale for intensive longitudinal studies. *Assessment, 29*(6), 1301–1319. https://doi.org/10.1177/10731911211008254
- **Purpose:** Instrument Validation
- **Methodology:** Experience Sampling, Instrument Validation, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** 20-item and 10-item Big Five state scales, BFI-2, NEO-PI-R, PANAS
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Personality Facet
- **Topic:** Personality, Psychometrics
- **Quality:** N = 1,041 (3 samples) | Structural: L | Three independent ILD samples, MEFA (CFI = .96). Between-person ω = .86, within-person ω = .51.
- **Notes:** First systematic psychometric evaluation of Big Five state scales for ILD. Five-factor structure at between- and within-person levels. Within-person reliability notably low, especially for Agreeableness.
### 362. Ringwald_2023.pdf
- **Citation:** Ringwald, W. R., Emery, L., Khoo, S., Clark, L. A., Kotelnikova, Y., Scalco, M. D., Watson, D., Wright, A. G. C., & Simms, L. J. (2023). Structure of pathological personality traits through the lens of the CAT-PD model. *Assessment, 30*(7), 2276–2295. https://doi.org/10.1177/10731911221143343
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** CAT-PD, PID-5, BFI-2, NEO-PI-3, IPIP-NEO-120, FI-FFM, IIP-SC
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** N = 3,987 (8 subsamples) | Structural: L | Large pooled sample (clinical + non-clinical), pre-registered, measurement invariance across gender/sample/race.
- **Notes:** Both 5- and 6-factor CAT-PD structures fit well and are invariant. Six-factor separates Anankastia from Disinhibition, supporting ICD-11. CAT-PD shows better discriminant validity than PID-5.
### 363. Ringwald_etal_2023.pdf
- **Citation:** Ringwald, W. R., Forbes, M. K., & Wright, A. G. C. (2023). Meta-analysis of structural evidence for the Hierarchical Taxonomy of Psychopathology (HiTOP) model. *Psychological Medicine, 53*(2), 533–546. https://doi.org/10.1017/S0033291721001902
- **Purpose:** Meta-Analysis
- **Methodology:** Meta-Analysis, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** Structured/semi-structured diagnostic interviews (23 DSM diagnoses)
- **Level of Detail:** Other (DSM diagnoses, psychopathology spectra)
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** N = 120,596 (35 studies, 48 samples) | Structural: XL | First quantitative meta-analytic test of HiTOP spectra. 5-factor model: CFI = .92, RMSEA = .07. Pre-registered.
- **Notes:** Five transdiagnostic dimensions (Internalizing, Detachment, Thought Disorder, Antagonism, Disinhibition) confirmed. Hierarchical structure: general p → Externalizing/Internalizing → further splits. PDs are strongest markers of the general factor.
### 364. ringwald_2024_hitop.pdf
- **Citation:** Ringwald, W. R., Abramovitch, A., Agelink van Rentergem, J. A., & Kotov, R. (2025). Do cognitive functions belong in the Hierarchical Taxonomy of Psychopathology (HiTOP) model? A meta-analysis. *Perspectives on Psychological Science, 20*(6), 1049–1064. https://doi.org/10.1177/17456916251347926
- **Purpose:** Meta-Analysis
- **Methodology:** Meta-Analysis, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** Neuropsychological tests (7 cognitive domains), structured diagnostic interviews (8 DSM disorders)
- **Level of Detail:** Cognitive Ability, Other (psychopathology superspectra)
- **Topic:** Neuroscience, Psychometrics
- **Quality:** N > 300,000 (80+ studies, 63 meta-analyses) | Structural: XL | Meta-analytic joint factor analysis integrating cognition and psychopathology.
- **Notes:** Cognitive functions do NOT form a separate domain — they integrate with psychoticism. Three superspectra: Psychoticism + Cognitive Dysfunction, Externalizing, Emotional Dysfunction. HiTOP's psychoticism superspectrum should include cognitive impairment.
### 365. ringwald_2025.pdf
- **Citation:** Ringwald, W. R. (2025). A call to action for explaining rather than merely predicting psychopathology. Unpublished manuscript, Department of Psychology, University of Minnesota.
- **Purpose:** Commentary/Editorial
- **Methodology:** Narrative Review
- **Instruments:** N/A
- **Level of Detail:** Other (psychopathology, mechanistic traits)
- **Topic:** Personality, Psychometrics
- **Quality:** Prestige: M | Unpublished manuscript. Well-developed conceptual argument. Not yet peer-reviewed.
- **Notes:** Argues dimensional models (including HiTOP) are actuarial risk models that predict without explaining dysfunction. Proposes "mechanistic traits" — stable person-environment dynamics assessed via intensive longitudinal designs.
### 366. Russell-Lasalandra_2026.pdf
- **Citation:** Russell-Lasalandra, L. L., & Golino, H. (2026). Prompt engineering for scale development in generative psychometrics. *arXiv preprint*. arXiv:2603.15909. https://doi.org/10.48550/arXiv.2603.15909
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Experimental/Intervention, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** AI-GENIE pipeline, GPT-4o, GPT-5.1, GPT-OSS-120B, GPT-OSS-20B, EGA
- **Level of Detail:** Item-Level, Personality Domain
- **Topic:** Psychometrics
- **Quality:** Structural: M | Thorough factorial simulation (4 models × 3 temps × 5 traits × 6 prompts × 100 reps). No human response data. Preprint.
- **Notes:** Adaptive prompting (conditioning on prior outputs) reduces item redundancy ~88–94% and improves structural validity. AI-GENIE reliably improves NMI. Prompt design is critical in generative psychometrics.
### 367. Samo_etal_2026.pdf
- **Citation:** Samo, A., Garrido, L. E., Abad, F. J., Golino, H., McAbee, S. T., & Christensen, A. P. (2026). Revisiting the IPIP-NEO personality hierarchy with taxonomic graph analysis. *European Journal of Personality, 40*(2), 369–390. https://doi.org/10.1177/08902070251352590
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** IPIP-NEO-300
- **Level of Detail:** Item-Level, Personality Facet, Personality Domain
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** N = 149,337 | Structural: XL | Very large sample, item-level bottom-up TGA. Single instrument (IPIP-NEO); single country; self-report.
- **Notes:** TGA recovers 3-level hierarchy: 28 facets, 6 traits (N, C, O, Sociability, Integrity, Impulsivity), 3 meta-traits (Stability, Plasticity, Disinhibition). Only 16/30 theoretical facets emerged. No general factor supported.
### 368. Thalmayer_etal_2024.pdf
- **Citation:** Thalmayer, A. G., Mather, K. A., Saucier, G., Naude, L., Florence, M., Adonis, T.-A., Shino, E. N., Asatsa, S., Witzlack-Makarevich, A., Bachlin, L. Z. M., & Condon, D. M. (2025). The cross-cultural big two: A culturally decentered theoretical and measurement model for personality traits. *Journal of Personality and Social Psychology, 128*(5), 1181–1208. https://doi.org/10.1037/pspp0000528
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis, Instrument Validation
- **Instruments:** Cross-Cultural Big Two Inventory (CCB2I; 45 items), IPIP IPC, QB6, SPI-27, IMHA
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** N = 2,496 (ALLS) + 61,760 (SAPA) | Structural: L | Multi-study, large combined N, cross-cultural (3 African + 13 countries). Scalar invariance not achieved; broad factors.
- **Notes:** Develops CCB2I measuring two cross-culturally ubiquitous factors (Communion/SSR and Agency/Dynamism) from 11 global lexical studies. Proposed as higher-level structure under which Big Five organizes.
### 369. vicentin_2026.pdf
- **Citation:** Vicentin, S., Granziol, U., Romano, D., Scandola, M., & Cona, G. (2026). The effect of age on the architecture of psychological and cognitive dimensions: A network perspective. *European Journal of Ageing, 23*, 10. https://doi.org/10.1007/s10433-025-00903-8
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Factor Analysis
- **Instruments:** NEO-FFI, Penn Emotion Recognition Task, Delay Discounting, NIH Toolbox Cognition Battery, ASR/OASR
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Cognitive Ability, Other (mental health)
- **Topic:** Neuroscience, Personality
- **Quality:** N = 681 (3 age groups) | Structural: M | HCP-YA and HCP-Aging data, EGA with bootstrap. Cross-sectional; modest n per group; domain-level personality only.
- **Notes:** Cognitive variables merge into single community in older adults (dedifferentiation). Emotion recognition and delay discounting migrate from cognitive to personality/mental-health community. Network global strength decreases with age.
### 370. vu_etal_2026.pdf
- **Citation:** Vu, H., Nguyen, H. A., Ganesan, A. V., Juhng, S., Kjell, O. N. E., Sedoc, J., Kern, M. L., Boyd, R. L., Ungar, L., Schwartz, H. A., & Eichstaedt, J. C. (2026). PsychAdapter: Adapting LLMs to reflect traits, personality, and mental health. *npj Artificial Intelligence, 2*, 26. https://doi.org/10.1038/s44387-026-00071-9
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Experimental/Intervention, Instrument Validation
- **Instruments:** PsychAdapter on Gemma-2B, GPT-2 Large, LLaMA-3-8B; Big Five (estimated from text); IPC
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Other (depression, life satisfaction)
- **Topic:** Personality, Psychometrics
- **Quality:** Structural: M | Novel method, 87.3% Big Five accuracy (human raters), 96.7% mental health. Generalizes across 3 LLMs and 2 text domains. No validation against standard inventories.
- **Notes:** PsychAdapter adds <0.1% parameters to base LLMs for personality-conditioned text generation. Human raters distinguish Low/Neutral/High personality at 87.3% accuracy. Applications: simulated patients, personality-congruent chatbots.
### 371. Wright_etal_2026.pdf
- **Citation:** Wright, A. G. C., Ringwald, W. R., Vize, C. E., Eichstaedt, J. C., Schwartz, H. A., Taxali, A., Angstadt, M., & Sripada, C. (2026). Assessing personality using zero-shot generative AI scoring of brief open-ended text. *Nature Human Behaviour, 10*(3), 541–555. https://doi.org/10.1038/s41562-025-02389-x
- **Purpose:** Original Research
- **Methodology:** Cross-Sectional, Experimental/Intervention
- **Instruments:** NEO-FFI, IPIP-NEO-120, CAT-PD, IIP-SC, 7 LLMs (ChatGPT 4.1, Claude 3.7, Gemini 2.5, Grok 3, Llama 4, Qwen 235B)
- **Level of Detail:** Personality Domain, Item-Level
- **Topic:** Personality
- **Quality:** N = 60 + 108 | Structural: L | Two independent samples, 7 LLMs, convergent r = .42–.48 (comparable to self-other agreement). Nomological network validation (profile r = .62–.96). Small Ns; novel method.
- **Notes:** Commercially available LLMs score Big Five from brief open-ended text (streams of thought, video diaries) without task-specific training. Average across 7 LLMs gives strongest convergence. Outperforms LIWC and bespoke ML models.
